## Section 001: Tdd Checkpoint Cadence Playbook
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Tdd Checkpoint Cadence Playbook", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed no seed line conveys that this theme holds a 61-line cadence contract carried byte-identically across two sweeps and two differently-named skills, the 202602 orchestrator and the 202604 retainer, five short sections that together answer when to checkpoint, how often, what an entry must contain, how to resume, and how to hand off
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Tdd Checkpoint Cadence Playbook", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the playbook exists because long sessions lose context faster than they lose code, and a fixed cadence converts memory preservation from a virtue into a schedule
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Tdd Checkpoint Cadence Playbook", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: treating checkpointing as a discipline of diligence rather than a triggered protocol leaves it to willpower, which is exactly the resource long sessions exhaust first

## Section 003: Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 003 "Pattern Scoreboard Ranking Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed three corpus-process rows stand where the playbook's own priorities rank, the trigger system leads, four event families that make checkpointing reactive to work shape rather than clock alone, then the execute-only-the-first-next-step resume rule, the playbook's sharpest and least obvious discipline, then the always-before-breaks frequency rule, the only trigger stated as unconditional

## Section 004: Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed generic corpus formulas stand where the playbook states its thesis in one opening line, use this cadence to prevent context drift in long sessions, naming drift, not loss, as the enemy, context does not vanish at once, it slides, and scheduled checkpoints are the correction pulses that keep the working model aligned with reality
- **supporting_reason:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because drift compounds silently because each small divergence between memory and code state seems ignorable until decisions start being made against a model that no longer exists
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the drift-blind failure is the confident wrong turn deep in a session, hours of work built on a remembered requirement the tests stopped reflecting long ago
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the thesis governs session-scale memory, project-scale knowledge management belongs to other themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the drift-prevention thesis and its mechanism, semantic triggers pulsing corrections at the moments models most likely diverge
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the four trigger families are exactly the four ways a session's mental model diverges from ground truth, phase flips change what done means, test changes change what true means, milestones change what exists, risk events change what is safe, so the trigger list is a taxonomy of drift sources wearing a scheduling costume
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 004 "Idiomatic Thesis Synthesis Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to treat every trigger event as a moment of probable divergence and checkpoint before proceeding on the new model

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed corpus-process bullets stand beside what the playbook implies for cadence failures, a missed checkpoint is repaired by an immediate catch-up entry marked late, not by retroactive fabrication at the missed timestamp, a broken resume, snapshot contradicting reality, halts next-step execution until reconciliation completes, and repeated misses of the same trigger family signal the trigger needs tooling support, not that the family is optional
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because cadence failures compound forward, a fabricated entry poisons every future resume that trusts it, so the repair rules privilege honest gaps over smooth-looking records

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed generic records stand beside what the cadence itself makes observable, the journal is a session's flight recorder, phase visible at every checkpoint, test surface visible through exact names, dependency state visible through blocker conditions, plan state visible through ordered next steps, and drift visible retroactively wherever a resume finds mismatch
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the cadence's entries are observability events for a system, the working session, that otherwise emits no telemetry at all, minds and agent contexts have no logs except the ones this practice writes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an unjournaled session is unobservable in the strict sense, its state reconstructible only from code diffs that show what changed but never what was believed, intended, or blocked
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: observability of sessions through the cadence, application observability belongs to the engineering themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the flight-recorder framing with the five visible surfaces, phase, tests, dependencies, plan, and drift
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the journal captures exactly the dimension version control cannot, git records what changed and the journal records why and what was believed at the time, so the pair forms a complete session record, code state from commits, mind state from checkpoints, and this corpus's practice of committing journals alongside content fuses the two records into one history

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed latency packet stands beside the playbook's own performance touchpoints, risk-event triggers fire on performance regression explicitly, and the handoff protocol's fifth item requires latest metrics if performance-sensitive, the cadence's two acknowledgments that performance state is part of session context worth preserving
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because performance context evaporates faster than functional context, a regression noticed but unjournaled is re-discovered from scratch by the next session, so the cadence names performance in both its trigger and handoff layers
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: handing off performance-sensitive work without the metrics item leaves the successor optimizing blind or, worse, unaware the work is performance-sensitive at all
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the cadence's performance-context rules, measurement methodology belongs to the system design theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the two touchpoints, regression as a first-class checkpoint trigger and metrics as a conditional handoff requirement

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed task-splitting bounds stand beside the playbook's own scale limits, the cadence governs one session's continuity and one handoff hop, it scales across long efforts by chaining sessions through snapshots rather than by growing entries, and its scope line bounds it to long sessions, short focused work pays the premium without the drift risk
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the chain design keeps every unit small, one entry per checkpoint, one snapshot per resume, one handoff per succession, so arbitrarily long efforts decompose into bounded links, this corpus's sixty-plus assignments being the local existence proof
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: scaling by entry growth instead, ever-longer entries summarizing ever-more history, makes snapshots unreadable exactly as they become most needed, the anti-scaling the chain design avoids
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: scale limits of the cadence, this evolution's own task splitting keeps the seed paragraphs
- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the chain model, bounded links over growing state, with the short-session exclusion and the corpus as the long-chain instance
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the latest-snapshot rule makes the chain Markovian by design, resume reads the latest snapshot, not the history, so each link must carry everything needed forward, which is precisely why the quality rules are strict, in a memoryless chain any dropped fact is dropped forever
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to keep entries link-sized, trust the latest snapshot as the complete resume state, and let long efforts be chains rather than sagas
